2. If all pilot VDTs are operational, both pilots will have an ADI selected at all times.
      19.2.1.1. The RALT OVRD function on the navigator/EWO E2 will only be used during
      day VMC or during combat/contingency operations.
  19.2.2. Change of Control. Pilot flying will initiate the change of control and state speed
  and steering reference when not following computer guidance. Pilot monitoring takes
  positive control of the aircraft and acknowledges the changeover.
  19.2.3. Altimeters. The pilot, copilot, and navigator will acknowledge all manual changes in
  altimeter setting. If TRUE ALT is selected, the navigator must still perform the required
  terminal area altitude calibrations. Crew members will monitor TRUE ALT altimeter
  settings for accuracy. The standby altimeters will be set to the lowest forecast altimeter
  setting for the route or area of operations. If TRUE ALT is selected, and the TRUE ALT
  altimeter setting falls below the lowest forecast altimeter setting, the TRUE ALT value will
  be set in the standby and used as the lowest altimeter setting for the route or area of
  operations. Use standby altimeters as the primary altitude reference when flying at
  MSA/ESA or obstacle warning reactions.
  19.2.4. Obstacle Procedures. Any tower or man-made obstruction within 3 NM of planned
  flight path must be positively identified visually or on radar. If not identified by 3 NM prior
  to the tower or obstacle, climb to at least 250 ft above the obstruction until clear.
  19.2.5. Terrain Following.
      19.2.5.1. The pilot monitoring will alert the crew, select the desired SCP and set the
      radar altimeter to 80% of SCP. After both pilots have selected TF and verified TF system
      tolerances are being met, they can intercept selected SCP after coordinating with the
      navigator or EWO. WARNING: Perform an in-flight check of the TF system, and a
      level or cresting check, when commencing low-level operations to ensure the system is
      operating within tolerances. If the TF system is flying out of limits low, TF operations
      will not be flown. If the TF system is flying out of limits high, TF operations are
      restricted to VMC. NOTE: Autopilot will not be used during low-level operations
  19.2.6. Visual, NVG, and Threat Penetration Low-level.
      19.2.6.1. Minimum visibility to conduct NVG low-level is 3 SM.
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                               151


      19.2.6.2. The pilot monitoring will use NVGs to clear during NVG low-level operations.
      19.2.6.3. Set the RALT TF function to the desired altitude, no less than 300 ft (100 ft for
      threat penetration operations). The radar altimeter will be set to no lower than 80% of
      this altitude.
      19.2.6.4. Prior to accepting any update, the navigator will inform the pilots by stating
      "Updating" followed by a heading or clearance to follow computer steering.
      19.2.6.5. Following each update, time and conditions permitting, the navigator will
      determine which navigation mode is most accurate (INS/GPS, INS1, INS2, GPS, etc.)
      and make the appropriate selection.
   19.2.7. Turn point procedures and Off Course Maneuvering.
      19.2.7.1. The navigator or EWO will provide the new course and MSA prior to the turn
      point. The EWO will brief anticipated threats and aircraft deviations for the next leg.
      19.2.7.2. The navigator and pilot monitoring share the primary responsibility of clearing
      terrain in the direction of turn and no other duties must be allowed to interfere with this
      responsibility.
      19.2.7.3. Use caution whenever maneuvering in excess of 2 NM from the planned flight
      path, as terrain in the immediate area may exceed the MSA and terrain masking may be
      rendered ineffective. NVG altitudes may also be inadequate for the unexpected flight
      path.
19.3. Low-level Emergency Procedures.
   19.3.1. Unplanned Obstacle Warning (OW) Reactions. WARNING: These procedures are
   not written to allow crews to ―visually‖ clear themselves while reacting to a TF system
   generated OW. Sound judgment and clear crew communication needs to be exercised
   throughout the execution of these maneuvers to quickly resolve the cause of an unplanned
   OW, regardless of its validity.
      19.3.1.1. Straight ahead corridors. The pilot flying will increase power towards max TIT
      (not to exceed 19,600 inch/pounds torque), initiate a positive G pull-up (to attain a pitch
      approaching CLA) and begin a climb towards MSA, while the pilot monitoring, navigator
      and EWO cross-check all other available means to identify the cause of the OW. The
      navigator/EWO directing the navigation will provide lateral guidance/direction in
      response to the determined cause of the OW. The flying pilot will resume flying the
      system after receiving confirmation from the navigator/EWO directing the navigation the
      TF system is functioning properly (i.e., no radar system fails or pointing errors).
      19.3.1.2. Course correction and turning corridors. If the OW occurs as a result of
      exceeding 10 degrees angle of bank, the pilot flying will immediately lessen the bank to
      less than 10 degrees while executing the steps outlined in 19.3.1.1
          19.3.1.2.1. If the cue returns after the reduction in bank angle to less than 10 degrees,
          the pilot flying will resume flying the system (i.e., no radar system fails or pointing
          errors).
          19.3.1.2.2. If the OW remains after the reduction in bank angle to less than 10
          degrees, the crew will continue with the procedures outlined in 19.3.1.1
 152                                                AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


   19.3.2. Planned OW Reactions. Crews will thoroughly brief and positively identify a safe
   altitude, distance to go and intended crew actions for the OW during preflight planning and
   route study. Crews should also discuss actions to be taken if the OW occurs differently than
   planned.
   19.3.3. Avionics/Aircraft Systems Failure. When a failure of the selected TF system or
   other required equipment occurs or is suspected during IMC low-level operations, the pilot
   will immediately begin a climb to at least MSA for the leg or segment and select another
   low-level method (if available). Maintain the MSA until the malfunction is corrected and
   continued safe low-level operations can be resumed. When the failure cannot be corrected
   and an alternate low-level method is not available, discontinue low-level operations.
   WARNING: It is essential to verify terrain clearance prior to deselecting Radar TF. In IMC,
   do not deselect TF if the cue is directing a climb.     CAUTION: Due to possible system
   damage, do not use the X OVRD, KU OVRD and SPC OVRD keys on the navigator/EWO
   E2 layer except during actual combat or contingency operations.            NOTE: Weather
   conditions can reduce the effectiveness of mission-essential sensors to the point of effective
   failure. If this occurs, comply with the appropriate emergency procedures.
   19.3.4. Engine Failure.
       19.3.4.1. Discontinue low-level operations if feasible.
       19.3.4.2. If terrain following is necessary, select the X-band radar TF/TA mode if
       available, verify the system is in the three-engine TF mode and check the route of flight
       for obstacles which could exceed available climb performance.
19.4. Airdrop Operations.
   19.4.1. The engineer runs all airdrop checklists and will operate the flaps.
   19.4.2. MC automatic CARP/HARP, manual (visual) CARP/HARP, manual beacon and
   GMRS methods may be used to position the aircraft at the release point.
   19.4.3. Normally navigate to the DZ using MC guidance. The navigator may decide at any
   time to accomplish the drop visually, using NVGs if necessary. For GMRS airdrops, the
   pilot will visually position the aircraft and call the release.
   19.4.4. The MSL altitude used on the drop leg must be the true altitude for the drop (block 3
   on AF Form 4015) if the MC BALT setting is derived by in-flight altimeter calibration. If
   using a preflight altimeter use the indicated MSL altitude (block 8 on AF Form 4015).
   19.4.5. All controlled ETA procedures should be completed prior to reaching the slowdown
   point. Early or delayed slowdown calls or "S" turns after the IP for timing purposes should
   be avoided. After the slowdown, airspeed changes for TOT control should be avoided.
   19.4.6. After the IP. Upon departing the IP (or the slowdown point if one is programmed),
   the navigator, EWO, and pilots will confirm the MC is on a DROP or HARP leg. The pilot
   will steer to the CARP/HARP using the flight director system or follow the navigator's
   headings.
   19.4.7. Slowdown. Unless otherwise briefed, reduce power to 1,000 in-lbs of torque and
   depending on the tactical situation, maintain altitude or climb immediately. As airspeed
   permits, extend flaps to 50%, slowing to drop airspeed. If descent is required, reduce power
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                                153


   to 1,000 in-lbs of torque and maintain level flight. As airspeed permits, extend flaps to 50%
   and descend while maintaining 140 KCAS.
   19.4.8. The use of the TERM CNST function should be reserved for operations where terrain
   will cause an OW throughout the objective run-in or an OW in close proximity to the
   objective area; but in all cases its use will be thoroughly briefed. The pilot flying will retain
   radar TF cues or select TERM CNST as briefed, while flying the navigator‘s briefed True or
   Barometric Altitude, Magnetic Course, and Calibrated Airspeed. The pilot monitoring
   should retain radar TF cues and backup the pilot flying. Terrain or threat conditions may
   require a different location for leaving en route low-level altitudes and this will be prebriefed
   if planned. The navigator will cross-check the MC CARP/HARP display with the manual
   CARP/HARP.           WARNING: The mission computer will command a descent if TERM
   CNST is selected above the programmed leg altitude. The DROP leg altitude could be below
   the minimum en route altitude for the terrain, weather, and degraded equipment conditions
   actually encountered. Prior to selection of TERM CNST, careful evaluation of all sensors (or
   visual references), should be made to ensure the mission computer guidance will not direct
   the aircraft into terrain.
   19.4.9. A thorough study of the terminal environment will be conducted to identify the most
   suitable VDT radar altimeter setting for the airdrop being accomplished.
      19.4.9.1. When dropping in flat and rolling terrain, set VDT radar altimeter to 50 ft
      below briefed drop AGL altitude for personnel airdrops and no lower than the minimum
      chute actuation altitude for equipment airdrops.
      19.4.9.2. When dropping in sloped or mountainous terrain, set the VDT radar altimeter
      to 50 ft below the briefed CARP radar altitude for personnel airdrops. Set the VDT radar
      altimeter to the lowest expected terrain crossing altitude for equipment airdrops.
19.5. SCA Procedures.
   19.5.1. Crew Duties. NOTE: Normally the copilot flies the SCA and the pilot assumes
   control for the landing. During NVG operations, an NVG landing qualified pilot (non-
   instructor) may takeoff and land from the right seat provided an NVG landing qualified pilot
   is in the left seat and normal (non-assault) procedures are used. In this case, either pilot may
   fly the SCA, with the other pilot accomplishing the landing and subsequent takeoff.
   Instructor pilots may fly both the SCA and landing for demonstration purposes. During day
   operations or overt night operations to lit runways, either pilot may fly the SCA and landing.
      19.5.1.1. The navigator/EWO will determine the most accurate altimeter setting for the
      LZ using all available sources including GPS, weather forecasts, ground station reporting
      and altitude calibration, as available.
      19.5.1.2. Use this altimeter setting in the MC BALT. The standby altimeters will
      normally remain set at the lowest altimeter setting for the route or route segment.
      19.5.1.3. The flight engineer will have NVGs ready for immediate use. The PM will
      back up the PF on the displays and confirm terrain clearance using all means available.
      The PM and flight engineer will clear for obstacles and other traffic.
   19.5.2. At the Initial Point.
154                                                  AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


      19.5.2.1. The navigator/EWO will verify final course guidance accuracy. The pilots,
      navigator, and EWO will confirm the system is in the APPR mode.
      19.5.2.2. The navigator or EWO will confirm LZ alignment with GM/PGM radar and
      IDS and give final headings as required.
  19.5.3. Slowdown.
      19.5.3.1. Slowdown should be initiated approximately 3 NM prior to the planned glide
      slope intercept point. The navigator/EWO will initiate the slowdown. The FE will state
      ―Tracking‖ once cleared for 50% flaps. When the flaps reach 50% and airspeed passes
      165 KIAS, the FE will state ―Landing Gear.‖ As soon as gear is down the FE will state
      ―Gear Down, Flaps‖ and standby for clearance to set flaps to 100%. Upon receiving
      clearance to move flaps, the FE will state ―Tracking‖ and resume the INFIL/EXFIL
      BEFORE LANDING checklist at the ―Landing Gear‖ step.
      19.5.3.2. Do not slow to threshold speed until established on final for both straight-in
      and turning SCAs. For turning SCAs, maintain 140 KCAS/KIAS or approach speed
      whichever is higher in the turn. Once the slowdown is initiated, no further airspeed
      corrections for TOA control should be made.
  19.5.4. Altimeters. The pilot will set the radar altimeter to the MDA (HAT). Throughout
  the approach, the pilot will monitor radar/barometric altimeters to ensure appropriate terrain
  clearance until taking over for the landing. WARNING: The obstacle clearance procedures
  in this chapter are not applicable to NVG operations conducted in a visual pattern. The pilot
  must maintain visual contact with the LZ and with surrounding terrain in order to execute a
  successful approach.
  19.5.5. One Mile Prior to Glide slope Intercept.
      19.5.5.1. When approaching the glidepath (or prebriefed distance to go), the navigator or
      EWO will clear the pilots to select TERM CNST after cross-checking all available
      sensors for significant terrain. The copilot will select TERM CNST after receiving
      clearance/confirmation from the pilot of adequate terrain clearance. WARNING: The
      navigator will verify the actual aircraft position is inside the planned SCA obstacle
      template prior to initiating descent (and prior to pilots selecting terminal consent).
  19.5.6. Glide slope Intercept. The pilot flying will begin descent following the flight
  director cue unless directed otherwise by the navigator/EWO, pilot, or flight engineer. The
  pilot flying will not descend the aircraft below MSL MDA. WARNING: The PM,
  navigator, and EWO must closely monitor radar altimeters to ensure accuracy of altimeter
  settings to prevent inadvertently flying below planned AGL minimums.
      19.5.6.1. At glide slope intercept the navigator or EWO will monitor course and glide
      slope deviation using the VSD or HSD display. Report deviations greater than 50 yd
      laterally or 50 ft vertically, along with an advisory as to whether the aircraft is correcting
      to, paralleling or diverging from course/glidepath.
  19.5.7. Level Off/Minimums.
      19.5.7.1. Level off at MDA if the pilot monitoring has not taken control of the aircraft.
      The flying pilot will maintain the MDA until the pilot monitoring takes control of the
      aircraft or until reaching the MAP (system position distance-to-go is 0.0 or as briefed by
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                                155


     the navigator or EWO). The pilot monitoring may direct the flying pilot to the LZ
     (remain at/above MDA) or may maneuver the aircraft himself. The navigator or EWO
     will select the IDS, if available, in FPV mode and MED FOV after completing the final
     position update and verifying the runway has been correctly identified and is clear of
     obstructions.
     19.5.7.2. IMC/VMC SCA. Do not descend below MDA until the touchdown zone is
     visually identified and confirmed by both pilots.
  19.5.8. Visual Acquisition of the LZ.
     19.5.8.1. The flight engineer will assist in field acquisition and visually check the LZ is
     clear.
     19.5.8.2. Aircraft lighting will be as briefed/directed by ground parties for authentication
     purposes. The use of covert lighting will be thoroughly briefed in respect to threat,
     runway environment, and authentication procedures.
  19.5.9. After Touchdown.
     19.5.9.1. The copilot and flight engineer will assist the pilot in locating the off-
     load/onload point once taxi speed is reached and clear for other aircraft and obstructions.
     If the pilot makes the landing from the right seat, the pilot in the left seat will be prepared
     to assume aircraft control once taxi speed is reached.
  19.5.10. Go-around Procedures.
     19.5.10.1. The navigator or EWO will advise the pilots upon arriving at the MAP and
     repeat the terrain clearance altitude (e.g., radar TF SCP, RALT TF, MSL altitude, pattern
     altitude, etc.), the initial heading, and will call altitudes climbing through from 50 ft to
     200 ft AGL (i.e., 50, 100, 150, 200) if a go-around is executed.
     19.5.10.2. The flight engineer will monitor engine instruments, airspeed, altitude, rate of
     climb, configuration, and terrain clearance.
     19.5.10.3. Go-around-Immediate Landing Feasible. The pilot will state "Go-Around,
     Immediate Landing Feasible." After establishing a safe climb, the pilot flying will direct
     the flaps set to 50%. The pilot flying will call for 100% flaps before or after rolling off
     the perch and call for the appropriate checklist. The engineer will pick up the checklist
     by reconfirming the landing gear position and accomplishing the remaining items of the
     checklist. Maintain 140 KCAS/KIAS or approach speed, whichever is higher until
     established on final.
         19.5.10.3.1. This maneuver should only require the movement of flaps and landing
         light switches. If any other change in configuration is accomplished, then the entire
         checklist will be used.
         19.5.10.3.2. The go-around button will be activated if terrain near the airfield dictates
         use of TF to safely fly visually back to the runway. The pilot's decision to use the go-
         around button should be coordinated with the navigator and EWO during preflight
         planning. WARNING: Be aware after G/A is selected, radar TF will not be active,
         nor will lateral steering begin until the selected SCP is reached.      WARNING: If
         G/A is not selected and the system remains in the APPR leg, the pilot must fly the
 156                                                 AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


          MSL altitude directed by the navigator to ensure terrain clearance. The cue will not
          give reliable vertical guidance until reestablished on the glide slope.
          19.5.10.3.3. If the GO-AROUND button was selected, TERM CNST must be
          selected prior to descending below the selected SCP to prevent a LOW ALT.
   19.5.11. Takeoff Procedures.
       19.5.11.1. Accomplish the ON THE RUNWAY portion of the INFIL/EXFIL checklist.
       If a visual pattern or turning SCA back to the LZ is to be accomplished, use the ON THE
       RUNWAY touch and go steps of the INFIL/EXFIL checklist, if desired. Use the normal
       checklist procedures IAW applicable T.O. 1C130(MDS)-1, when not using the
       INFIL/EXFIL checklist.
       19.5.11.2. The navigator will provide a departure heading, altitude, and terrain
       considerations. NOTE: For departures into TF en route procedures, the navigator will
       program an APPR leg on the ground to ensure the selection of G/A results in an active TF
       system with valid steering.
       19.5.11.3. The pilot flying will make the takeoff wearing NVGs. The pilot monitoring
       will wear NVGs and be prepared to fly the planned departure on NVGs or transition to
       instruments and fly the navigator‘s directions in the event of NVG failure.
       19.5.11.4. Use IR taxi and landing lights to the minimum extent required to maintain
       visual references during takeoff roll. Interior lighting is the same as for the approach and
       landing. The flight engineer will clear the LZ for obstacles.
       19.5.11.5. Use normal takeoff performance unless max effort performance is required.
       At refusal speed, the copilot calls "Go." At takeoff speed, the copilot calls "Rotate." If
       takeoff and refusal speed are equal, the copilot will call "Go."
       19.5.11.6. At takeoff speed, the pilot will rotate the aircraft to establish a positive climb
       rate. The copilot checks the pitch attitude and will raise the landing gear on the
       command of the pilot after ensuring a positive rate of climb. The flight engineer will
       back up the pilot using NVGs during climb out. The copilot may take control of the
       aircraft if directed by the pilot and continue the climb out to the egress route altitude.
       The pilot flying directs the accomplishment of the appropriate AFTER TAKEOFF
       checklist.
          19.5.11.6.1. At or before takeoff speed, the pilot will select MC G/A mode.
       19.5.11.7. The navigator or EWO will advise the pilots of the initial on course heading
       and call altitudes climbing through from 50 ft to 200 ft AGL (i.e., 50, 100, 150, 200).
       19.5.11.8. As soon as conditions permit, the loadmaster will check equipment restraint
       and condition/needs of the onboard user.
19.6. Defensive Maneuvering.
   19.6.1. When operating in VMC, pilots must clear terrain prior to and during any threat
   reaction.
   19.6.2. When operating in IMC, the EWO or navigator will use the GM or PGM to clear for
   terrain prior to calling a turn or break that requires a faster turn rate than the radar turning
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                            157


   scan capability. In IMC, the navigator may clear the pilot up to a 30-degree bank angle using
   this method. The pilots/navigator/EWO will cross-check their altitude references to ensure
   the aircraft is not descending during the maneuver.       WARNING: Practicing defensive
   threat maneuvering does not constitute authority to deviate from limitations in the flight
   manual.
19.7. Collision Avoidance Operations.
   19.7.1. Operate the GCAS in the tactical mode (AUDIO ON or VISUAL ON) during non-
   TF low-level operations (RALT TF or dual terminal consent airdrops).
19.8. Tanker, Air-to-Air Refueling (HAAR/TAAR) Restrictions.
   19.8.1. Minimum equipment. An operational Air-to-Air TACAN is the minimum electronic
   equipment required to complete an electronic HAAR/TAAR.
   19.8.2. Minimum Safe Altitude (MSA). Heading and altitude must provide at least 1,000 ft
   of clearance above all obstacles within 5 NM of course to be flown in non-mountainous
   terrain, 2,000 ft of clearance in mountainous terrain.
   19.8.3. Minimum visibility for a visual rendezvous is 3 NM and 1 NM for electronic
   rendezvous.
   19.8.4. Unless directed otherwise by a specific exercise operations order/plan, in
   contingencies, or during emergency fuel situations, communication capability between
   tankers and receivers will be maintained during all normal rendezvous and air refueling
   operations. Voice transmissions, however, will be IAW the emission option used.
   19.8.5. Unplanned HAAR/TAAR tracks will be coordinated between tanker and receiver to
   ensure adequate in-flight mission planning and terrain clearance. Crews will compute and
   relay MSA and recommended refueling altitude prior to join-up on any unplanned
   HAAR/TAAR track.
   19.8.6. A loadmaster will be positioned at each paratroop door, or on each side of the ramp
   when refueling with ramp and door open.
   19.8.7. Unless an emergency fuel condition exists, receiver crews will not attempt probe to
   drogue contact in a turn at night. Once in contact, turns are permitted.
19.9. Radar Trail Procedures.
   19.9.1. Type and Size. Radar trail formation is normally flown in two or three ship
   elements, with each successive element separated by one minute. The squadron CC/DO may
   authorize 20 second spacing between elements for phases of the mission where reduced
   separation is required.
   19.9.2. Weather Minimums. For takeoff and landings as a formation, weather in the
   terminal area should allow for VMC operations; however, if required, minimum visibility is
   1 SM (RVR 0500). IMC rejoins or extended IMC flight is not authorized during training.
   Radar trail procedures may be used to penetrate IMC to regain VMC for mission
   accomplishment.
   19.9.3. Altitudes. Comply with Chapter 17 altitude restrictions. Threat Penetration is not
   authorized during peacetime in radar trail formation.
158                                               AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


  19.9.4. Aircraft Lighting. If preceding aircraft have other than full external lighting, all
  crews will use NVGs. Formation and position lights set to dim, lower anticollision light and
  the IR rotating beacon on, are required for NVG formation operations in an ATC
  environment. Also, see AFI 11202V3 AFSOC Sup.
  19.9.5. Takeoff Intervals. For interval takeoffs, the minimum spacing is 15 seconds between
  aircraft. For simultaneous departures, aircraft separation must be at least 3,000 ft between
  aircraft. Lead must have at least 3,500 ft of useable runway for takeoff.
      19.9.5.1. Acceleration. Use a common reference for formation acceleration (e.g., time or
      geographic point). If elapsed time is used, begin timing when lead starts takeoff roll.
  19.9.6. En route Rejoin Procedures.
      19.9.6.1. General. No more than three aircraft will rejoin at the same geographic point.
      Plan to rejoin 30 seconds in trail then close to the briefed spacing (no closer than 20
      seconds).
      19.9.6.2. Rejoin Abort. If a crew determines they will miss their rejoin TOA by greater
      than 10 seconds, they will inform lead. The late aircraft will climb to a predetermined
      MSL altitude (threat allowing) and attempt to join the formation as soon as possible, but
      prior to the IP. Follow briefed instructions if proper formation position cannot be
      established prior to the IP. If any aircraft experiences aircraft/equipment problems just
      prior to the rejoin, they may elect to rejoin at the end of the formation or proceed to a
      suitable recovery airfield. Remaining aircraft within the formation will reposition as
      instructed by the formation leader to close the formation.
  19.9.7. En route Procedures.
      19.9.7.1. Airspeed/Groundspeed Changes. Airspeed and groundspeed changes should
      occur at the same geographic point referenced by a navigation reference point (NRP).
      Use timed spacing off of serial lead as a backup or when NRP is unavailable. This
      ensures proper timed spacing is maintained.
      19.9.7.2. Formation Positioning. Formation navigators will plan and brief the latest
      allowable time to a turn point and the subsequent actions to be taken if this time cannot
      be made. NOTE: Using PGM at high altitude will result in increased spacing due to the
      slant range computations. TA and weather (WX) presentations will reflect the actual
      aircraft in-trail position.   NOTE: During high level ops, formation aircraft may use
      autopilot to relieve crew task loading. Autopilot during low-level ops will not be used.
  19.9.8. Formation Airdrops. For visual formation airdrop spacing, see Chapter 17. Normal
  radar trail airdrop spacing is 20 second trend dot spacing for all high-speed and 50% flap
  setting drops. During contingencies, close-interval CDS/CRS airdrops may be flown using
  less than 30 second trend dot spacing with Group Commander/COMAFSOF approval. 30
  second trend dot spacing equates to the 6,000 ft spacing requirement outlined in Chapter 17.
  19.9.9. Formation Air Refueling. Lead aircraft is responsible for weather avoidance during
  the rendezvous until 0.5 NM from contact position. Any aircraft in the formation may advise
  the formation of inclement weather on the refueling track.
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                                159


                                           Chapter 20

                         MC130P EMPLOYMENT PROCEDURES

20.1. General. This chapter describes the specific equipment requirements and restrictions for
MC130P Combat Shadow employment. It provides directives for aircraft employment and
operational procedures found in AFTTP 33.MC130, AFTTP 31., and other instructions. In the
case of any conflict between AFTTP and this regulation, AFI 112MC130V3 takes precedence.
20.2. Minimum Operating Equipment. Refer to Table 20.1, Tactical Operations, for
minimum tactical equipment. Aircrew experience level and the mission scenario may dictate
greater equipment requirements than those listed.

Table 20.1. Tactical Operations.
      Event           Radar      Navigation Solution 1       Pilot’s       Navigator’s       IDS
                                                            RADALT          RADALT
 Day LL                                   I-DOP 2             X2
 NVG LL                   X2              I-INS or            X2
 (Mountainous)                       I-DOP & GPS 2
 NVG LL (Non-          X 2, 5             I-INS or               X2                           X5
                                                    2
 Mountainous)                        I-DOP & GPS
 IMC LL                    X            GPS FOM-2                X
 Threat                                   I-INS or               X              X             X4
 Penetration                          I-DOP & GPS
 VMC SCA                                   I-DOP                 X              X
 IMC SCA                   X            GPS FOM-2                X              X
 Covert NVG                            I-INS or GPS              X              X
 Landing
 Blacked-Out                           I-INS or GPS              X              X             X3
 NVG Landing
 VMC Airdrop                      I-DOP, I-INS, or GPS           X
 IMC Airdrop               X            GPS FOM-2                X              X
 HAAR/TAAR                                                       X6
 Notes:
 1. Navigator‘s integrated display computer unit (IDCU) must be operational.
 2. Aircraft that do not meet this requirement are restricted to MSA or to the in-trail (directly
 behind lead, stacked high) position in a formation.
 3. If IDS is inoperative, must have SCNS G-I submode.
 4. IDS required for night overland penetrations.
 5. Must either have an operational radar or IDS for non-mountainous NVG LL.
 6. If refueling altitude is below 3,000 ft AGL.
   20.2.1. Degraded Systems Restrictions/Procedures. Degraded Systems Training (DST) is
   used to prepare crews to accomplish the mission simulating certain pieces of equipment
   inoperative (or intentionally turned off for emission control). Specifically, DST serves the
   purpose of training, via simulation of inoperative equipment. Designate DST route segments
160                                                 AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


  during the route brief. DST will not be performed by inexperienced crews, and will be taken
  into consideration during the ORM assessment. The following restrictions and procedures
  are designed to maximize training and safety.
      20.2.1.1. DST Specific Restrictions:
      20.2.1.2. PICs will brief the equipment simulated as inoperative, aircrew coordination,
      crew duties, and disorientation/emergency procedures prior to flight.
      20.2.1.3. Visibility must be at least 5 SM in mountainous terrain.
      20.2.1.4. Illumination: Effective illumination must be greater than 10% or DST must be
      conducted between the forecasted hours of sunset and estimated end of nautical twilight
      (EENT). Effective illumination must be greater than 25% if a safety observer is not
      aboard IAW paragraph 20.2.1.9 Otherwise, DST may be conducted between the
      forecasted hours of sunset and EENT.
      20.2.1.5. Equipment/Personnel Requirements:
      20.2.1.6. Radar Altimeter. The aircraft‘s radar altimeter must be operational and on
      during the entire flight. Additionally, both pilot and navigator indicators must be fully
      functioning.
      20.2.1.7. Ground Mapping/Weather Radar. The radar must be fully functional before
      flight. The navigator will function check the radar periodically during DST NVG low-
      level operations to verify functionality. If at any time during the function check it is
      determined that the radar will not sufficiently provide terrain avoidance, DST operations
      will be discontinued. At this time tactical operations will revert to restrictions provided
      in Table 20.1.
      20.2.1.8. Navigation equipment. The SCNS INS or GPS must be operational and on
      during DST. A GPS moving map laptop with PFPS and DTED installed may be
      employed by the navigator. DTED coverage should encompass the planned flight area
      and data within 25 NM of all course centerline.
      20.2.1.9. Personnel: A mission qualified instructor pilot must be at the controls. A
      mission instructor/evaluator navigator must be on board. The instructor/evaluator
      navigator, if not manning the navigator position, will be acting in an instructor/evaluator
      capacity. Restriction: During NVG low-level radar denied DST operation, a second
      mission qualified navigator (or mission qualified pilot) will act as the safety observer, and
      will monitor the progress of the mission using NVGs. The scanner will wear NVGs and
      carry an additional low-level chart.
  20.2.2. Procedures:
      20.2.2.1. Single Radar Altimeter operations. For single radar altimeter operations the
      navigator‘s radar altimeter repeater only will be placed to off and the pilot monitoring
      and flight engineer will assume all responsibilities for radar altimeter altitude calls
      referencing the pilot‘s radar altimeter as directed by the PIC. Equipment/Personnel
      requirements must be met IAW paragraph 20.2.1.5
      20.2.2.2. Radar denied operations. The radar will be placed in the standby position
      during NVG low-level, radar denied operations in order to simulate an
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                              161


      inoperative/unavailable radar. A safety observer will be on board IAW paragraph
      20.2.1.9 Having the radar in standby will allow a quick transition to normal NVG low-
      level procedures during limited visibility or in emergency situations (inadvertent weather
      penetration, emergency climb, etc.). The navigator will turn on the radar any time cloud
      cover degrades effective illumination in flight. Equipment/Personnel requirements must
      be met IAW paragraph 20.2.1.5
      20.2.2.3. Simulated SCNS denied/degraded operations.               Simulated SCNS
      denial/degradation maybe accomplished during any phase of flight regardless of the
      illumination. Additionally, any crew position integrated display computer unit (IDCU)
      may be dimmed.          The crews primary navigational references become the
      copilots/navigator‘s charts and moving map PFPS. If any crew member becomes
      disoriented an immediate climb to ESA must be accomplished. Equipment/Personnel
      requirements must be met IAW paragraph 20.2.1.5
20.3. En route Operations.
   20.3.1. The pilot and copilot may share a single low-level chart during flight. If this option
   is used, both the pilot and copilot must participate in pre-mission route analysis using the
   single chart.
20.4. Airdrop Operations.
   20.4.1. SCNS Airdrop (AD)/Troop Jump (TJ) Computer-Manual Select Switch must be set
   to AD/TJ manual.
   20.4.2. The Radar Altimeter will be set to no lower than 50 ft below planned drop altitude
   EXCEPTION: High Altitude Airdrops.
   20.4.3. High-speed operations with the paratroop doors open will not be accomplished
   during training missions.
   20.4.4. A maximum of six static line parachutists may be deployed out a paratroop door that
   has a Benson tank installed on that side. Consideration should be given to the amount of
   equipment each parachutist will carry.
   20.4.5. IMC Air Drops.
      20.4.5.1. IMC Airdrop Procedures. The following procedures may be practiced in VMC.
      IMC airdrop from the MC130P requires OG/CC approval.
      20.4.5.2. IMC Drop Altitude. Fly minimum IMC drop altitudes at 500 ft above the
      highest obstruction to flight (man-made obstruction, terrain feature, or spot elevation), or
      400 ft plus one contour interval above the highest depicted terrain contour, whichever is
      highest, within 3 NM either side of the run-in centerline from DZ entry point to DZ exit
      point or as specified in AFI 11231, whichever is higher. The IMC drop altitude may be
      segmented per AFTTP 33.MC130(U).
      20.4.5.3. DZ Entry Point. Formation descent will not begin until the last aircraft is at or
      past the DZ entry point. The DZ entry point is a fixed point on DZ run-in course where
      an aircraft or formation of aircraft may safely begin descent from IMC en route altitude
      to IMC drop altitude. The DZ entry point is a maximum of 40 NM prior to the DZ exit
      point according to Federal Aviation Administration FAR exemption 4371C. Formation
 162                                                AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


       descent will not begin until the last aircraft in the formation is at or past the DZ entry
       point.
       20.4.5.4. DZ Exit Point. The DZ exit point is a fixed point on the DZ escape flight path
       centerline, established during pre-mission planning, at which the formation will be at the
       minimum IMC en route altitude. Calculate the exit point based upon three-engine
       performance at airdrop gross weight. This point will be planned no less than 4 NM track
       distance beyond the DZ trailing edge.
       20.4.5.5. Earliest Descent Point (EDP). The earliest descent point is the earliest point on
       the DZ run-in course where the lead aircraft may begin IMC descent to IMC drop altitude
       and be assured of terrain clearance for the entire formation. Compute EDP by subtracting
       formation length from the computed DZ entry point.
       20.4.5.6. In IMC, drop clearance is confirmed via radio call or beacon acquisition.
       20.4.5.7. To position the aircraft accurately at the release point, use the following
       pilot/navigator procedures:
       20.4.5.8. Upon departing the IP (or the slowdown point if one is programmed), the LN
       and pilots will confirm that the Airdrop leg and sensitive steering are active. Normally
       navigate to the DZ using SCNS guidance. Once on final run-in course, position updates
       will correct steering information supplied to the flight directors. The LN will confirm LZ
       alignment with radar and IDS if available and provide final headings off steering if
       required. The pilot flying will steer to the CARP/HARP using the flight director system
       or follow the navigator's headings. The LN will confirm SCNS position using
       preplanned update points and provide corrections if required. Normally, the LN will
       provide course guidance, distance to go, and drift information approximately every mile
       during the run-in. The RN must be prepared at any time along the run-in to assume
       navigation, make all required calls, and accomplish the drop visually using NVGs if
       capable.
       20.4.5.9. At the release point: The pilot monitoring and the LN will confirm the aircraft
       is positioned within the pre-briefed visual safety box during VMC operations. Both
       pilots and both navigators will confirm the aircraft is positioned within the pre-briefed
       IMC safety box (i.e., ± 200 yds, ± 3 secs) for IMC operations.
20.5. SCA Procedures.
   20.5.1. IMC SCA Procedures. The following procedures may be practiced in VMC. IMC
   SCAs require OG/CC approval.
   20.5.2. Ensure the radar is operational, no less than a GPS of FOM-2, and a system update
   and altimeter update are conducted within 10 minutes of starting the IMC SCA.
   20.5.3. IMC SCA Altitude. Fly minimum IMC SCA altitudes at 500 ft above the highest
   obstruction to flight within 2 NM either side of the run-in centerline from 10 NM or IP to
   Begin Descent point whichever is closer to the LZ. The IMC SCA altitude may be
   segmented.
   20.5.4. Crew Duties.
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                            163


     20.5.4.1. The pilot flying will steer to the LZ using the flight director system or follow
     the navigator's headings. The LN will confirm SCNS position using preplanned update
     points and provide corrections if required. The right navigator will confirm LZ centerline
     alignment on short final using all available means and correct aircraft alignment if
     required.
     20.5.4.2. The navigator will determine the most accurate altimeter setting for the LZ
     using all available sources including GPS, weather forecasts, ground station reporting and
     altitude calibration, as available. Normally, navigate to the LZ using SCNS guidance.
     Once on final run-in course, position updates will correct steering information supplied to
     the flight directors.
     20.5.4.3. The flight engineer will have NVGs ready for immediate use. The PM will
     back up the PF on the instruments/displays and confirm terrain clearance using all means
     available. The PM and flight engineer will clear for obstacles and other traffic.
  20.5.5. At the Initial Point.
     20.5.5.1. The left navigator will make distance calls at every mile inside ten miles and
     every half mile inside three miles (or as briefed).
     20.5.5.2. The left navigator will confirm LZ alignment with radar and IDS and give final
     headings as required.
  20.5.6. Slowdown.
     20.5.6.1. Slowdown should be initiated approximately 3 NM prior to the planned glide
     slope intercept point. The navigator will initiate the slowdown.
     20.5.6.2. Do not slow to threshold speed until established on final for both straight-in
     and turning SCAs. For turning SCAs, maintain 140 KIAS or approach speed whichever
     is higher in the turn. Once the slowdown is initiated, no further airspeed corrections for
     TOA control should be made.
  20.5.7. Altimeters. Radar altimeters should remain set at en route altitude setting until
  slowdown. Once slowdown is initiated, the radar altimeters may be reset as briefed. The left
  navigator will set 300 ft to guard against shallow glide slopes. WARNING: The obstacle
  clearance procedures in this chapter are not applicable to NVG operations conducted in a
  visual pattern. The pilot must maintain visual contact with the LZ and with surrounding
  terrain in order to execute a successful approach.
  20.5.8. Approaching Glide slope Intercept.
     20.5.8.1. Approaching glide slope intercept, the navigator will confirm the accuracy of
     the barometric altimeter setting by comparing actual AGL and MSL altitudes with those
     depicted on the SCA template. WARNING: The navigator will verify that the actual
     aircraft position is inside the planned SCA obstacle template prior to initiating descent.
     20.5.8.2. Glide slope Intercept. The pilot flying will begin descent upon navigator
     direction unless directed otherwise by the navigator, pilot, or flight engineer. The pilot
     flying will not descend the aircraft below MSL MDA. WARNING: The PM, LN, and
     RN must closely monitor radar altimeters to ensure accuracy of altimeter settings to
     prevent inadvertently flying below planned AGL minimums.
164                                                 AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


      20.5.8.3. At glide slope intercept the left navigator will state ―Begin Descent‖ and repeat
      the desired initial descent rate. The left navigator, backed up by the RN, will provide
      glidepath advisories referenced from navigator‘s pressure and radar altimeters backed up
      by SCNS. These calls will be made at ½ NM intervals until reaching the ―100 Ft‖ or
      ―Minimums‖ call. State deviations in excess of 150 explicitly. The left navigator also
      advises the pilot if the aircraft is correcting to or diverging from glidepath and how
      rapidly if appropriate.
  20.5.9. Level Off/Minimums.
      20.5.9.1. Do not descend below MDA until the LZ environment is identified visually and
      confirmed by both pilots. Whoever identifies the LZ first will call ―Zone In Sight,‖
      relative clock position and any discrepancies (i.e., lights out, etc.). Both pilots will then
      confirm the zone and cross-check the alignment for the proper heading.
      20.5.9.2. VMC SCA. Do not descend below 100 ft until the touchdown zone is visually
      identified and confirmed by both pilots.
      20.5.9.3. IMC SCA. Do not descend below 300 ft until the LZ environment is positively
      identified on the IDS. Do not descend below 200 ft until the LZ environment is visually
      identified and confirmed by both pilots.
  20.5.10. Visual Acquisition of the LZ.
      20.5.10.1. The flight engineer will assist in field acquisition and visually check the LZ is
      clear.
      20.5.10.2. Aircraft lighting will be as briefed/directed by ground parties for
      authentication purposes. The use of covert lighting will be thoroughly briefed in respect
      to threat, runway environment, and authentication procedures.
  20.5.11. After Touchdown. The copilot and flight engineer will assist the pilot in locating
  the off-load/onload point once taxi speed is reached and clear for other aircraft and
  obstructions. If the pilot makes the landing from the right seat, the pilot in the left seat will
  be prepared to assume aircraft control once taxi speed is reached.
  20.5.12. Go-Around Procedures.
      20.5.12.1. The left navigator calls ―Missed Approach Point‖ at zero to go on the SCNS
      and repeat the terrain clearance altitude (e.g., MSL altitude, pattern altitude, etc.), the
      initial heading, and will call altitudes climbing through from 50 ft to 200 ft AGL (i.e., 50,
      100, 150, 200) if a go-around is executed.
      20.5.12.2. The flight engineer will monitor engine instruments, airspeed, altitude, rate of
      climb, configuration, and terrain clearance.
      20.5.12.3. Immediate Landing Feasible. The pilot will state "Go-Around, Immediate
      Landing Feasible." After establishing a safe climb, the pilot flying will direct the flaps
      set to 50%. The pilot flying will call for 100% flaps before or after rolling off the perch
      and call for the appropriate checklist. The engineer will pick up the checklist by
      reconfirming the landing gear position and accomplishing the remaining items of the
      checklist. Maintain 140 KIAS or approach speed, whichever is higher until established
      on final.
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                               165


          20.5.12.3.1. This maneuver should only require the movement of flaps and landing
          light switches. If any other change in configuration is accomplished, then the entire
          checklist will be used.
   20.5.13. Takeoff Procedures.
      20.5.13.1. Accomplish the ON THE RUNWAY portion of the INFIL/EXFIL checklist.
      If a visual pattern or turning SCA back to the LZ is to be accomplished, use the ON THE
      RUNWAY touch and go steps of the INFIL/EXFIL checklist, if desired. Use the normal
      checklist procedures IAW applicable T.O. 1C130(MDS)-1, when not using the
      INFIL/EXFIL checklist.
      20.5.13.2. The navigator will provide a departure heading, altitude, and terrain
      considerations.
      20.5.13.3. The pilot flying will make the takeoff wearing NVGs. The pilot monitoring
      will wear NVGs and be prepared to fly the planned departure on NVGs or transition to
      instruments and fly the navigator‘s directions in the event of NVG failure.
      20.5.13.4. Use IR taxi and landing lights to the minimum extent required to maintain
      visual references during takeoff roll. Interior lighting is the same as for the approach and
      landing. The flight engineer will clear the LZ for obstacles.
      20.5.13.5. Use normal takeoff performance unless max effort performance is required.
      At refusal speed, the copilot calls "Go." At takeoff speed, the copilot calls "Rotate." If
      takeoff and refusal speed are equal, the copilot will call "Go."
      20.5.13.6. At takeoff speed, the pilot will rotate the aircraft to establish a positive climb
      rate. The copilot checks the pitch attitude and will raise the landing gear on the
      command of the pilot after ensuring a positive rate of climb. The flight engineer will
      back up the pilot using NVGs during climb out. The copilot may take control of the
      aircraft if directed by the pilot and continue the climb out to the egress route altitude.
      The pilot flying directs the accomplishment of the appropriate AFTER TAKEOFF
      checklist.
      20.5.13.7. The left navigator will advise the pilots of the initial on course heading and
      call altitudes climbing through from 100, 200, and 300 ft AGL.
      20.5.13.8. As soon as conditions permit, the loadmaster will check equipment restraint
      and condition/needs of the onboard user.
20.6. Tanker (HAAR/TAAR)-Receiver Air Refueling.
   20.6.1. The pilot in control of the airplane during air refueling operations with the autopilot
   engaged will keep one hand on the control column and the other hand available for
   immediate throttle operation, in order that prompt action can be taken in the event of an
   autopilot malfunction.
20.7. Formation Restrictions.
   20.7.1. Rejoins. Minimum altitude for rejoin is 500 ft AGL.
   20.7.2. En route. Minimum lateral spacing is 200 ft for visual formation, 1 NM for radar
   trail.
 166                                                 AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


                                           Chapter 21

                         MC130W EMPLOYMENT PROCEDURES

21.1. General. This attachment describes the specific equipment requirements, training
restrictions, and regulatory guidance for MC130W Combat Spear employment. This chapter is
not a stand-alone reference and should be used in conjunction with the rest of this instruction, the
AFTTP series, and other directives. In the case of any conflict between the AFTTP series and
this instruction, this instruction takes precedence.
   21.1.1. Terminology. Joint terminology will be used for mission planning and execution.
   Crew members will have a working knowledge of the information contained in the following
   publications: JP 303, Doctrine for Joint Interdiction Operations; JP 309.1, Joint Laser
   Designation Procedures (JLaser); JP 309.3, Joint Tactics, Techniques, and Procedures for
   Close Air Support (CAS). Crew members will also maintain a working knowledge of
   AFTTP(I) 32.6, JFIRE, Multi-Service Tactics, Techniques, And Procedures For The Joint
   Application Of Firepower (JFIRE).
   21.1.2. Control of Classified Information and Materials. It is the responsibility of every
   crew member to control the classified material they use. This includes maps/charts with
   target coordinates, friendly positions, battle lines, or threat positions drawn on them. Most
   imagery, target lists, Command Electronic Order Information (CEOI), SPINS, rules of
   engagement (ROE), and strike data are classified and must be controlled and handled as such.
   Imagery from the sensor systems that has been recorded must be handled IAW the
   appropriate security classification guide.
21.2. Aircrew Complement. Information in this section augments the guidance provided in
Chapter 3 of this instruction. MC130W aircrew complement for basic and mission sorties will
be IAW Table 21.1 and the following:
   21.2.1. Pilots. When required, supervision for 30MM and SOPGM live/dry-fire operations
   may be accomplished by a standing instructor provided both seats are occupied by at least
   basic qualified pilots.
   21.2.2. Navigator and CSO.
       21.2.2.1. Unit/mission commanders may authorize local basic flights without a navigator
       when not required for mission accomplishment.
       21.2.2.2. A single navigator may be considered a full mission complement for all
       mobility events.
       21.2.2.3. For AAR and HALO only the navigator or CSO performing the event needs to
       be certified in the event.
       21.2.2.4. On local training sorties, maximum effort and NVG takeoffs and landings
       conducted from the VFR pattern, tactical recoveries (excluding SCAs), and FARP may
       be accomplished without a navigator or CSO onboard.
       21.2.2.5. Unit/mission commanders may authorize local mission training flights without
       a CSO when manning or systems limitations dictate. In this case, live fire operations
       (30MM or SOPGM) are not authorized.
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                             167


      21.2.2.6. MOP supervision. A noncurrent navigator or CSO may be supervised by an
      instructor occupying the other MOP position. An unqualified navigator or CSO requires
      a standing instructor. If both the navigator and CSO are unqualified, two standing
      instructors are required.
   21.2.3. Loadmasters.
      21.2.3.1. Two LMs or one LM and another qualified crew member are required when 40
      or more passengers are being carried (except during contingencies and unit moves). Both
      crew members must remain in the cargo compartment.
      21.2.3.2. Two LMs are required on all mission sorties with the following exceptions:
          21.2.3.2.1. On personnel airdrops if only one paratroop door will be opened or when
          performing free-fall drops below 13,000 ft MSL.
          21.2.3.2.2. Non-tactical on/off-load of equipment or personnel.
          21.2.3.2.3. During hot refuel/FARP receiver operations (LM will perform panel
          operator duties).
          21.2.3.2.4. One instructor and two students are considered full mission complement
          on local training sorties.
          21.2.3.2.5. When approved by unit/mission commanders, armed overwatch local
          training sorties may be conducted with a single LM. In this case, live fire operations
          (30MM or SOPGM) are not authorized.
   21.2.4. Direct Support Operator. DSOs are added to the crew as required.

Table 21.1. MC130W Crew Complement.
       Crew Position             Basic        Augmented          Mission        Augmented
                                                Basic                            Mission
 Pilot/PIC                         1              2                  1              2
 Copilot                           1              1                  1              1
 Navigator                         1              2                  1              2
 Combat Systems Operator           -              -                  1              2
 Flight Engineer                   1              2                  1              2
 Loadmaster                        1              2                  2              2
 Direct Support Operator           -              -                  1              1
21.3. Minimum Operating Equipment. Refer to Table 21.2, Tactical Operations, for
minimum tactical equipment requirements. Aircrew experience level and mission scenario may
dictate greater equipment requirements than those listed.

Notes:
1. The navigator‘s IDCU must be operational.
2. During local VFR pattern training only the pilots‘ radar altimeters are required.
3. If both sensors are inoperative, must have SCNS G-I sub-mode.
4. Not required for airdrops above 3,000 ft AGL.
5. Coarse/Acquisition Miniaturized Integrated GPS/INS Tactical System (C-MIGITS).
6. Advanced Tactical Navigation (ATACNAV) inertial navigation unit.
7. Need at least one operative sensor with an operative laser designator.
  21.3.1. Degraded Systems Training. DST is used to prepare crews to accomplish the
  mission simulating certain pieces of equipment inoperative or intentionally turned off for
  emission control.
      21.3.1.1. The equipment simulated as inoperative, aircrew coordination, crew duties, and
      disorientation/emergency procedures will be briefed prior to flight.
      21.3.1.2. For terminal area operations in mountainous terrain, visibility must be at least 5
      SM, and the pilot and navigator radar altimeters must be operational and on.
      21.3.1.3. During SCNS degraded operations the radar must remain operational and on.
      21.3.1.4. A mission instructor must be in either a pilot or navigator/CSO position.
      21.3.1.5. The SCNS INS or GPS must be operational and on during DST. IDCUs and
      flight director mode switches can be positioned to simulate the INS and/or GPS
      inoperative.
      21.3.1.6. DST Procedures.
         21.3.1.6.1. Radar denied operations. The radar will be placed in the standby position
         to simulate an inoperative/unavailable radar. Having the radar in standby will allow a
         quick return to normal procedures during limited visibility or in emergency situations
         (inadvertent weather penetration, emergency climb, etc.). When operating at low
         altitude, do not place the radar in standby if cloud cover degrades effective
         illumination.
         21.3.1.6.2. SCNS degraded operations. Simulated SCNS degradation may be
         accomplished during any phase of flight regardless of the illumination. The flight
         director mode switches can be positioned to simulate the INS and/or GPS inoperative
         or the navigator may select a degraded SCNS sub-mode via the IDCU. Additionally,
         any crew position IDCU may be dimmed. The crew‘s primary navigational
         references become the copilot/navigator charts, Brimstone, and moving map PFPS.
         21.3.1.6.3. C-MIGITS failure. Simulate C-MIGITS failure by turning it off. VMC
         required.
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                              169


21.4. Not Used.
21.5. En route Operations.
   21.5.1. Operations below 3,000 ft AGL are considered low-level operations. Crews will
   comply with all applicable low-level procedures and restrictions given in Chapter 17.
   21.5.2. Altimeter Updates.     Update locations will be briefed during route study and
   verbalized in-flight.
   21.5.3. Radar Altimeter. During armed overwatch, radar altimeters will be set per crew
   discretion but should not be lower than 3,000 ft.
   21.5.4. GCAS. Normal mode (audio and visual on) will be used during armed overwatch.
   21.5.5. ETCAS. Use the Above, below, and Normal settings as appropriate for the phase of
   flight and mission. The Below setting should be used for tactical descents.
21.6. SCA.
   21.6.1. SCAs are used to place the aircraft on final approach, properly configured, in a
   position to identify the landing area and complete a landing. SCAs are performed using the
   INFIL/EXFIL checklist. The FE reads the INFIL/EXFIL checklist. When the tactical
   situation dictates flying an instrument approach while utilizing the INFIL/EXFIL checklist,
   ensure all briefing items from Step 2 of the normal DESCENT checklist are covered in the
   crew briefing during the ENROUTE portion of the INFIL/EXFIL checklist.
   21.6.2. Order of Battle (OB) Analysis. The enemy OB (actual or simulated) is the most
   important factor in determining the route of flight to and from the LZ, including the location
   of the initial point (IP). Plan a minimum 10 NM straight-in approach unless prohibited by
   the OB. The type and direction of recovery should be varied (threat and airspace permitting)
   to avoid a predictable recovery pattern from day–to-day.
   21.6.3. Plan to intercept a 3-degree glide slope no later than one mile from touchdown unless
   terrain or obstructions dictate otherwise.
   21.6.4. A full SCA plate for the landing runway is required. The navigator will construct an
   approach plate using the SCA Creator 3.1, AF Form 4118, or an OGV-approved planning
   form. Copilots will carry plates for all preplanned SCAs.
   21.6.5. Chart Preparation. Use the largest scale chart available from 10 NM inbound. A
   1:50,000 chart is preferred, but in no case will it be smaller than 1:250,000. The navigator
   will select update points for the SCNS and altimeter. Charts will include the following items:
   IP; slowdown point; descent point; and the missed approach, departure, and go-around paths.
   Ensure update points for the SCNS and altimeter are annotated. It is of utmost importance to
   have sufficient, reliable position and altitude update points prior to the IP and final run-in.
   21.6.6. SCA Procedures.
      21.6.6.1. These procedures are based on the copilot flying the SCA and the pilot
      assuming control for the landing. During NVG operations, an NVG landing qualified
      pilot (non-instructor) or copilot may takeoff and land from the right seat provided an
      NVG landing qualified pilot is in the left seat and normal (non-assault) procedures are
      used. In this case, either pilot may fly the NVG SCA, with the other pilot accomplishing
170                                                AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


      the landing/takeoff. Refer to Chapter 9 for touch and go restrictions. Instructor pilots
      may fly the entire approach and make the landing for demonstration purposes. For
      approaches and landings not requiring NVGs (day operations or overt night operations to
      lighted runways) either the pilot or copilot may fly the approach and accomplish the
      landing. EXCEPTION: Mission qualified instructor pilots may perform maximum
      effort landings/takeoffs from the right seat.
      21.6.6.2. SCA Coordination. During training missions with no onboard user involved,
      the PIC will determine and brief the time warnings (60-, 30-, 20-10-, 6-, and 1-minute)
      required for the mission. The pilot and navigator will brief the SCA using the appropriate
      aircrew mission briefing guide during the ENROUTE portion of the INFIL/EXFIL
      checklist. Additional briefing items may be added, as required, for the particular mission.
      NOTE: During training missions with no onboard user, time warnings may be deleted
      during multiple approaches. When an onboard user is involved, time warnings may be
      compressed with user concurrence.
      21.6.6.3. Twenty Minutes Prior to Landing.
         21.6.6.3.1. The navigator will determine the most accurate QNH altimeter setting for
         the LZ using all available sources including GPS, weather forecasts, ground station
         reporting, and altitude update, as available. Use this altimeter setting in SCNS.
         21.6.6.3.2. If required, the FE will close the blackout curtains and install eyebrow
         window curtains, and all crew members will set lighting for NVG operations.
         21.6.6.3.3. Each pilot will silently ensure both positions on their NVG battery packs
         are operational.
         21.6.6.3.4. Landing light usage will be briefed in the pre-mission brief and during the
         INFIL/EXFIL ENROUTE checklist.
         21.6.6.3.5. The copilot will check the LZ data in SCNS using approved sources (the
         SCA plate, Form 70, Pilot’s Flight Plan and Flight Log, and FLIP approach plate if
         available). NOTE: At least one pilot will monitor the SCNS airborne radar approach
         (ARA) page for glide slope cross-check. NOTE: Terrain permitting, at the IP the
         navigator will sequence steering to the approach leg in order to roll out on final
         course guidance without overshooting. Once on final approach, position updates will
         correct steering information supplied to the flight directors.
      21.6.6.4. Slowdown Procedures. Approximately 3 NM prior to the planned glide slope
      intercept point, the navigator will initiate the slowdown by stating "Slowdown,
      Slowdown, Now." Once the slowdown is initiated, no further reduction in airspeed for
      TOA control should be made.
         21.6.6.4.1. The pilots and navigator will set their radar altimeters to the MDA
         (HAT).
         21.6.6.4.2. The PF will slow the aircraft to no less than normal 50% threshold speed,
         configure the flaps and gear as airspeed permits, and call for the appropriate checklist.
         The PF will call for 100% flaps as airspeed permits and slow to normal or max effort
         threshold speed.
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                           171


        21.6.6.4.3. The FE will state ―Tracking‖ once cleared for 50% flaps. When the flaps
        reach 50% and airspeed passes 165 KIAS the FE will state ―Landing Gear‖. As soon
        as gear is down the FE will state ―Gear Down, Flaps‖ and standby for clearance to set
        flaps to 100%. Upon receiving clearance to move flaps, the FE will state ―Tracking‖
        and resume the INFIL/EXFIL BEFORE LANDING checklist at Step 3, ―Landing
        Gear.‖
        21.6.6.4.4. The FE will check that the gear is down and flaps are set as required and
        verify the hydraulic panel is set to the proper configuration. When the FE calls
        ―Landing Light Panel‖ the FE will verify the landing lights are extended and off or as
        briefed. NOTE: When slowdowns are initiated further out than 3 NM prior to glide
        slope intercept, consider maintaining 140 KIAS (or approach speed, whichever is
        higher) and delaying the call for 100% flaps until 1 NM prior to glide slope intercept.
     21.6.6.5. Glide Slope Intercept.
        21.6.6.5.1. Approaching glide slope intercept, the navigator will confirm the
        accuracy of the barometric altimeter setting by comparing actual AGL and MSL
        altitudes with those depicted on the SCA template. WARNING: The navigator will
        verify that the actual aircraft position is inside the planned SCA obstacle template
        prior to initiating descent.
        21.6.6.5.2. At 50 ft below glide slope intercept, the navigator will state "Begin
        Descent," and repeat the desired initial descent rate. The navigator will monitor glide
        slope deviation using the SCNS ARA display and provide glidepath advisories with
        reference to the SCNS, the navigator‘s pressure altimeter, and the radar altimeter.
        The navigator will report deviations greater than 50 ft along with an advisory as to
        whether the aircraft is correcting to, paralleling, or diverging from glide path or
        course. The PM will back up the PF on the SCNS/instrument displays and ensure the
        M1 sensor is selected on the 9 inch monitor to aid in visually identifying the LZ. The
        CSO will back up the navigator on all required calls and aid in visual acquisition of
        the LZ.
        21.6.6.5.3. When the navigator calls ―1 Minute‖ or ―2 Miles‖ the LM will notify
        cargo compartment personnel that there is ―1 Minute‖ to landing.
        21.6.6.5.4. The PF will descend following the navigator‘s direction and the SCNS
        ARA information.
            21.6.6.5.4.1. VMC SCA. Do not descend below 100 ft until the touchdown zone
            is visually identified and confirmed by both pilots.
            21.6.6.5.4.2. IMC SCA. Do not descend below 300 ft until the LZ environment
            is positively identified on M1 or M2 sensor. Do not descend below 200 ft until
            the LZ environment is visually identified and confirmed by both pilots.
        21.6.6.5.5. The navigator, backed up by the PM, will advise the crew at 100 ft above
        MDA and at MDA by stating ―100 Above‖ and ―Minimums.‖ The PF will
        acknowledge the call and level the aircraft at MDA. Execute a go-around if the
        runway is not in sight at the MAP or if a safe landing cannot be made.
172                                                AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


         21.6.6.5.6. When the navigator calls ―Minimums‖ the LM will notify cargo
         compartment personnel to "Prepare to Land."
         21.6.6.5.7. The CSO will verify that the runway has been correctly identified and is
         clear of obstructions using the M1 or M2 sensor prior to reaching runway threshold.
         CAUTION: The M2 sensor will be stowed prior to touchdown. Both sensors will
         remain powered on for landing.
      21.6.6.6. Visual Acquisition of the LZ (usually within 2 NM).
         21.6.6.6.1. The first crew member to identify the LZ will call ―Runway In Sight‖ and
         give the clock position and any discrepancies noted (i.e., any lights out, etc.).
         21.6.6.6.2. The PM, upon visual acquisition of the LZ states ―Runway In Sight‖ and
         may direct the copilot to the LZ (remain above MDA) or may maneuver the aircraft
         to LZ alignment. The PM will ensure that the PF and navigator understand that the
         PM has taken over the responsibility for directing the aircraft.
         21.6.6.6.3. The FE should verbally clear the LZ by stating ―Runway In Sight,
         Runway Appears Clear‖ if duties allow.
         21.6.6.6.4. At the ―100 Above‖ call, the FE will state ―Lights‖ and the PM will state
         ―On‖ or as briefed.
         21.6.6.6.5. Transfer of aircraft control for the landing may occur anytime after the
         landing pilot has positively identified the touchdown point.
         21.6.6.6.6. After the transfer, the PM will monitor airspeed, descent rate, and bank
         angle. The PM will advise the PF if descent rate exceeds 1,000 FPM (or as briefed
         for a steeper glide slope) or if bank angle exceeds 15 degrees. The navigator will
         monitor the radar altimeter and glide slope and will notify the pilot of deviations
         greater than 50 ft along with an advisory as to whether the aircraft is correcting to,
         paralleling, or diverging from glide slope.
         21.6.6.6.7. No later than 100 ft AGL, the navigator will begin to provide HAT calls.
         Each HAT call will be followed by an airspeed call from the PM. The navigator will
         provide a 10 ft call.
      21.6.6.7. After Touchdown.
         21.6.6.7.1. All available crew members will assist the pilots in scanning during
         ground operations. Upon reaching a safe taxi speed the M2 sensor can be returned to
         normal operations to assist in scanning.
         21.6.6.7.2. When the aircraft is stopped at the on/off-load location, the pilot will give
         the LM clearance by stating "Clear To On/Off-load." Dim interior NVG lighting
         when practical. If the flight deck and cargo compartment curtains are drawn, the
         navigator may maintain sensor/IDCU video for follow-on flight planning. Do not
         move the aircraft until the LM calls "Clear To Taxi." When there is a delay in the
         on/off-load or an extended ground time is anticipated, raise the ramp approximately
         12 inches above the ground so the aircraft can taxi in the event of an emergency.
         21.6.6.7.3. The departure airfield control officer (DACO) should not clear personnel
         or equipment to board the aircraft until cleared by the LM. Vehicles will be driven
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                          173


        onto the aircraft. The LM will coordinate with the DACO to confirm that all
        personnel and equipment are aboard and onload is complete.
        21.6.6.7.4. Touch and go operations are authorized during INFIL/EXFIL operations
        with or without the use of NVGs. Complete the BEFORE LANDING portion of the
        INFIL/EXFIL checklist on the initial approach to the runway and transition to the ON
        THE RUNWAY touch and go steps of the INFIL/EXFIL checklist after touchdown.
        After the first touch and go, the touch and go steps of the INFIL/EXFIL checklist
        (* items) may be used. The crew will continue using normal SCA approach and
        landing procedures. The navigator may make calls as briefed by the PIC during
        visual patterns when established on downwind and the AFTER TAKEOFF touch and
        go steps of the INFIL/EXFIL checklist are complete. Time warnings are not
        required. Complete the full AFTER TAKEOFF portion of the INFIL/EXFIL
        checklist on the last departure from the airfield. WARNING: The obstacle clearance
        procedures in this chapter are not applicable to NVG operations conducted in a visual
        pattern. When conducting a visual pattern, the pilots must maintain visual contact
        with the LZ and with surrounding terrain in order to execute a successful approach.
     21.6.6.8. Go-around Procedures.
        21.6.6.8.1. General. Do not descend below the MDA until the LZ is in sight and the
        landing pilot has taken control of the aircraft (if required). A go-around is required
        when the LZ is not in sight at the MAP (SCNS distance-to-go is zero or as briefed by
        the navigator) or a safe landing cannot be made. If landing is desired, the crew may
        fly a visual pattern back to landing (Immediate Landing Feasible) or proceed to the IP
        for another approach.
        21.6.6.8.2. The navigator will advise the pilots upon arrival at the MAP and repeat
        the MSL altitude and initial heading required and will call altitudes during the climb
        until above cruise altitude. The navigator will call every 50 ft to 300 ft AGL, then
        every 100 ft until ―lights out.‖
        21.6.6.8.3. The FE will back up the pilots on engine instruments, airspeed, altitude,
        rate of climb, configuration, and terrain clearance.
        21.6.6.8.4. Immediate Landing Feasible. The PF will state "Immediate Landing
        Feasible." After establishing a safe climb, the PF will direct the flaps set to 50%.
        Once the go-around is established, the pilot closest to the runway will normally fly
        the pattern. The landing pilot may take control of the aircraft at any time. The PF
        will call for 100% flaps before or after rolling off the perch and call for the
        INFIL/EXFIL BEFORE LANDING checklist. The FE will resume the checklist at
        Step 2. The CSO will use available sensors to increase the crew‘s situational
        awareness by providing clock position and distance calls to the runway as well as aid
        in terrain/obstacle avoidance. CAUTION: Pilots are more susceptible to spatial
        disorientation during NVG go-arounds and departures.
     21.6.6.9. Takeoff Procedures
        21.6.6.9.1. Accomplish the ON THE RUNWAY portion of the INFIL/EXFIL
        checklist. If a visual pattern back to the LZ is to be accomplished, use the ON THE
        RUNWAY touch and go steps of the INFIL/EXFIL checklist, if desired. Use the
 174                                                AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011


          normal checklist procedures IAW T.O. 1C130(M)W1, Section II, when not using the
          INFIL/EXFIL checklist procedures.
          21.6.6.9.2. The navigator will provide a departure briefing including: heading,
          altitude, terrain and obstacles. CAUTION: The M2 sensor will be stowed for
          takeoff. It can be returned to normal operation when airborne.
          21.6.6.9.3. Lighting will be configured as required by the tactical situation.
       21.6.6.10. Loss of NVGs:
          21.6.6.10.1. On Approach. If the PF or PM lose use of their NVGs inside of 1 NM,
          perform a go-around or as briefed. If the FE loses use of NVGs, land at the discretion
          of the PIC.
          21.6.6.10.2. On the Ground. The pilots will transfer aircraft controls and continue
          takeoff/landing roll or reject as briefed. The FE will be prepared to turn on overt
          lighting at the direction of the PIC in the event of NVG failure during takeoff or
          landing roll.
          21.6.6.10.3. After takeoff. Continue the climb out and follow the appropriate
          procedures for loss of NVGs.
21.7. Tactical Recovery.
   21.7.1. Tactical recoveries include the random steep, random shallow, overhead, and
   downwind. The approach and landing is a visual maneuver backed up with SCNS, sensors,
   and radar.
   21.7.2. Slowdown points will be planned and briefed for all tactical recoveries.
   21.7.3. Unless briefed otherwise, the PF will call the slowdown for all tactical recoveries.
21.8. High Altitude Airdrop.
   21.8.1. The MC130W conducts personnel military free-fall (MFF) high altitude low opening
   (HALO) and high altitude high opening (HAHO) airdrops in VMC or IMC.
   21.8.2. DZ Survey Review. The pilots, navigator, and CSO will review the point of impact
   (PI) location, DZ dimensions, 10-second warning location, airdrop safety box, and prominent
   DZ features.
   21.8.3. Airdrop Computations. During mission planning, the navigator will compute a
   HARP using AF Form 4015, AF Form 4017, or approved computer-aided HARP program.
   Both the navigator and CSO will verify the results. At the aircraft, the navigator will verify
   the actual number of jumpers and parachute type matches the planned HARP data.
   21.8.4. IMC Drop Altitude. The minimum IMC drop altitude is 500 ft above the highest
   obstruction to flight (man-made obstruction, terrain feature, or spot elevation), or 400 ft plus
   one contour interval above the highest depicted terrain contour, whichever is highest, within
   3 NM either side of the run-in course or as specified in AFI 11231, whichever is higher. The
   IMC drop altitude may be segmented.
   21.8.5. Airdrop Procedures. The FE will run the airdrop checklists and operate the flaps.
AFI11-2MC-130V3 22 DECEMBER 2011                                                            175


      21.8.5.1. Initial Point (IP). Terrain permitting, the navigator will sequence steering to
      the airdrop leg in order to roll out on final course guidance without overshooting.
          21.8.5.1.1. Departing the IP (or the slowdown point if one is programmed), the
